{"parentUuid":"b00598c9-8245-4b11-af42-37ae68221b86","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"3d0a0a14-0be7-4e95-aa54-2bdf558e0c8d","agentId":"ae79b3955f7bd98bd","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013VTWADGcmf7Cu1wgupMhha","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→# Writing the sequence\n     2→\n     3→## Phase 1: Client Information Gathering\n     4→\n     5→Before writing any sequences, collect **maximum information** from the client. Ideally, use an AI tool (like GPT-5) to generate a comprehensive questionnaire for outreach in their specific niche.\n     6→\n     7→### Key Questions to Ask:\n     8→\n     9→- **Who is the client?** (Company profile, industry, size)\n    10→- **Who is their ideal client?** (Demographics, psychographics, pain points)\n    11→- **Who is a bad fit client?** (Red flags, characteristics to avoid)\n    12→- **Who typically reaches out to them?** (Current client patterns)\n    13→- **Who do they want to attract?** (Target expansion)\n    14→- **Geographic data** (Location preferences, restrictions)\n    15→- **Demographics** (Gender, age, company size, etc.)\n    16→- **Any other relevant data** for database building, sequence descriptions, offers, etc.\n    17→\n    18→## Phase 2: AI-Assisted Project Analysis\n    19→\n    20→### Step 1: Generate JTBD and Roles\n    21→\n    22→After gathering all client data, upload everything to [Claude ai](https://www.notion.so/0899e6533b364080b603a284cfb15162?pvs=21) and ask it to study the project.\n    23→\n    24→**Key Positions & Roles:**\n    25→\n    26→- Which job titles are responsible for these decisions?\n    27→- What roles do we need to target?\n    28→\n    29→### JTBD\n    30→\n    31→Prompt:\n    32→\n    33→```\n    34→You are an expert Business Analyst specializing in identifying Jobs-To-Be-Done (JTBD) for B2B decision-makers. Your task is to analyze a company's offering and target customer profile to generate a comprehensive list of specific tasks, goals, and challenges that the target persona faces in their role.\n    35→\n    36→INPUT REQUIRED:\n    37→\n    38→**[PROJECT DESCRIPTION]:** Brief overview of the client's company, their solution/service, and core value proposition. Their website.\n    39→\n    40→**[IDEAL CUSTOMER PROFILE - ICP]:** Specific job title, role, industry, and company characteristics of the target decision-maker.\n    41→\n    42→YOUR TASK:\n    43→\n    44→Generate 5-8 specific JTBD items that this exact ICP faces in their daily work that directly connect to the client's solution. Each JTBD must be:\n    45→\n    46→- **Specific and Actionable** - Not vague pain points, but concrete tasks they need to accomplish\n    47→- **Role-Relevant** - Directly tied to their job responsibilities and KPIs\n    48→- **Solution-Connected** - Addressable by the client's offering\n    49→- **Business-Impact Focused** - Connected to measurable business outcomes\n    50→- **Current and Pressing** - Things they're actively dealing with, not hypothetical\n    51→\n    52→OUTPUT FORMAT:\n    53→\n    54→**[APPROVED JOBS-TO-BE-DONE - JTBD]:**\n    55→\n    56→1. [Specific operational task they need to complete]\n    57→2. [Goal they're trying to achieve with current limitations]\n    58→3. [Process they need to optimize or streamline]\n    59→4. [Challenge they're facing in their current workflow]\n    60→5. [Metric/KPI they're struggling to improve]\n    61→6. [Resource/time constraint they need to overcome]\n    62→7. [Compliance/risk management task they must handle]\n    63→8. [Strategic initiative they need to execute]\n    64→\n    65→EXAMPLE:\n    66→\n    67→**Project:** Professional moving services with loyalty program for commercial real estate management companies **ICP:** Property Manager at commercial real estate management companies\n    68→\n    69→**[APPROVED JOBS-TO-BE-DONE - JTBD]:**\n    70→\n    71→1. Earn commission through loyalty program referrals while providing value to tenants\n    72→2. Organize tenant relocations with minimal time investment to avoid distraction from core responsibilities\n    73→3. Adapt to changing moving schedules and renovation timelines without additional costs or delays\n    74→4. Provide high-quality moving services to tenants to increase satisfaction and retention rates\n    75→5. Streamline tenant move-in/move-out processes to reduce operational complexity\n    76→6. Ensure safe handling and transportation of tenant property to avoid damage claims and liability\n    77→7. Coordinate furniture and equipment relocations during office renovations without disrupting tenant operations\n    78→8. Improve tenant experience during transitions to enhance lease renewal rates\n    79→```\n    80→\n    81→### Step 2: Client Approval\n    82→\n    83→Present the JTBD and position list to the client for approval. Once confirmed, **responsibility shifts** - all future correspondence will be based on pre-approved information.\n    84→\n    85→## Phase 3: Sequence Creation with Claude\n    86→\n    87→Run these prompts in a \n    88→\n    89→### Email 1\n    90→\n    91→### Prompt\n    92→\n    93→```\n    94→You are a world-class B2B Outreach Strategist. Your expertise is in creating the **FIRST TOUCH EMAIL** that generates responses from busy decision-makers.\n    95→**[THE CONTEXT & TASK]** I will provide you with:\n    96→1. **[PROJECT DESCRIPTION]:** Brief overview of our client's company and offering\n    97→2. **[IDEAL CUSTOMER PROFILE - ICP]:** Specific job title and role we target\n    98→3. **[APPROVED JOBS-TO-BE-DONE - JTBD]:** Tasks, goals, challenges this ICP faces that our client solves\n    99→**[EMAIL #1 TEMPLATE - FILL THIS EXACT TEMPLATE]**\n   100→\n   101→`How are you currently {specific task from JTBD}?\n   102→\n   103→At {Company Name}, we {specific solution for their JTBD}. {Brief explanation how it works} + {concrete metric/proof}.\n   104→\n   105→Would you be open to a 15-minute call to explore how we can {solve their specific JTBD task}?`\n   106→\n   107→**[FILLING PRINCIPLES]**\n   108→\n   109→* Each sentence under 20 words\n   110→* Concrete numbers and metrics mandatory\n   111→* Brevity and Scannability: Short sentences (under 20 words), small paragraphs (1-3 sentences). Scannable in under 10 seconds.\n   112→* No Fluff: Skip clichés, buzzwords, formal language. Write like a helpful expert to a peer.\n   113→\n   114→**Example 1 (End-User - Crypto Avatar Platform):**\n   115→\n   116→- Company Info: website: coinavatar.com, content: A platform for users to create crypto avatars.\n   117→- **Good Output:**\n   118→\n   119→How are you currently managing royalty payouts to your avatar creators and handling payments from a global user base?\n   120→\n   121→At Inxy, we offer a powerful API to automate mass payouts and a simple Paygate for crypto acceptance, all under our EU/Canadian regulatory licenses.\n   122→\n   123→Would you be open to a 15-minute call to explore how we can streamline this for you?\n   124→\n   125→**Example 2 (Infrastructure Provider - Payment Gateway):**\n   126→\n   127→- Company Info: website: onchainpay.io, content: a crypto payment gateway.\n   128→- **Good Output:**\n   129→\n   130→As a crypto payment processor, how do you currently ensure regulatory compliance and operational resilience for your transaction flow?\n   131→\n   132→We provide a fully licensed (EU VASP/Canadian MSB) payment infrastructure that can act as a 'reliable backup partner' to enhance your service stability and compliance.\n   133→\n   134→Would a 15-minute strategic call to explore this be worthwhile?\n   135→```\n   136→\n   137→### Example\n   138→\n   139→```\n   140→You are a world-class B2B Outreach Strategist. for replies outside of SmartLead to ensure nothing is missed.\n   141→\n   142→**Why this works**:\n   143→\n   144→- Full visibility of all responses.\n   145→- Prevents missed warm replies.\n LinkedIn Setup\n     4→\n     5→### Sync with the Client\n     6→\n     7→Before starting any LinkedIn outreach campaign, align with the client regarding account usage. Sometimes, you will use the client's LinkedIn account, other times you will use your own. Discuss this upfront to ensure everyone is on the same page.\n     8→\n     9→**Important:**\n    10→\n    11→Before launching any campaign, always **check the SSI (Social Selling Index)**. Every time a campaign is launched, **notify the head of operations** with the current SSI and confirm the campaign is ready to go live. This ensures the account is in good standing and optimized for outreach. **Add the SSI to the \"SSI\" column in the client's Google Sheet** before creating the capacity plan.\n    12→\n    13→## 1. LinkedIn account rental\n    14→\n    15→**Use only with anti detect browsers adspower, gologin, dolphin anty**\n    16→\n    17→costs 135$, contact @a_trif in telegram\n    18→\n    19→### LinkedIn Premium Subscription\n    20→\n    21→Since LinkedIn accounts require a paid premium subscription, discuss the subscription cost with the client. **Ask them to provide the accounts directly or agree on a refund if you’re using your own.** Ensure this is clear from the beginning to avoid any surprises.\n    22→\n    23→### Handling Low SSI\n    24→\n    25→If you notice a low SSI, inform your client:\n    26→\n    27→‣ \n    28→\n    29→> “I noticed that your Social Selling Index decreased by 2 points (from 49 to 47). This may have happened because we sent a large number of invites, but only 20% were accepted.\n    30→> \n    31→> \n    32→> Since this is an important indicator for LinkedIn (affecting message limits and reducing the risk of being blocked), would you consider planning some content marketing activities on your page?\n    33→> \n    34→> It would be great if you could post on LinkedIn at least once a week.”\n    35→> \n    36→\n    37→[**LinkedIn Setup Guide**](https://www.notion.so/LinkedIn-1a5d8691cb46800ab298fa5bfa90558a?pvs=21)\n    38→\n    39→---\n    40→\n    41→## 2. Getsales Setup\n    42→\n    43→### Proxy Setup\n    44→\n    45→Each LinkedIn account must use its own dedicated proxy. This means buying one proxy per account and always logging in through that proxy — **no exceptions**. This helps keep the account healthy and avoids triggering LinkedIn’s security filters. Regularly track your SSI.\n    46→\n    47→[**Proxy Setup Guide**](https://www.notion.so/Proxy-f978e77cd31a4a17ad16cc5025ad4bc8?pvs=21)\n    48→\n    49→[Adding accounts to getsales](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=KXYp_eMlDoE&t=215s)\n    50→\n    51→### Connection Limit\n    52→\n    53→Never send more than **200 connections per LinkedIn account per week**. Exceeding this limit risks restrictions or even bans. Focus on **consistency over volume**. If your SSI is below 30, **limit connections to 100 per week**. \n    54→\n    55→## Adding the contacts\n    56→\n    57→1. Go to lists and create a list\n    58→\n    59→![image.png](LinkedIn%20outreach/image.png)\n    60→\n    61→![image.png](LinkedIn%20outreach/image%201.png)\n    62→\n    63→1. Go to import and click import accounts- select your list\n    64→    \n    65→    ![image.png](LinkedIn%20outreach/image%202.png)\n    66→    \n    67→2. Go to your automation and click add contatcs\n    68→    \n    69→    ![image.png](LinkedIn%20outreach/image%203.png)\n    70→    \n    71→3. Select your list and click select all \n    72→\n    73→![image.png](LinkedIn%20outreach/image%204.png)\n    74→\n    75→### How to filter contacts with less than 500 connections\n    76→\n    77→[Запись экрана 2025-10-30 в 13.33.45.mov](LinkedIn%20outreach/%D0%97%D0%B0%D0%BF%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%8C_%D1%8D%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0_2025-10-30_%D0%B2_13.33.45.mov)\n    78→\n    79→## Automation to google sheets\n    80→\n    81→[Getsales to sheets automation](LinkedIn%20outreach/Getsales%20to%20sheets%20automation%20257d8691cb468080b3daeab86dbf0739.md)\n    82→\n    83→For automating LinkedIn outreach, we use **Getsales**. This tool helps manage connection requests, follow-ups, and profile visits while keeping everything personalized.\n    84→\n    85→You can find the guides for Getsales here:\n    86→\n    87→[**Getsales YouTube Channel**](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCE-wJ2-PDodhHls8kVPx0BA/videos)\n    88→\n    89→- **Withdrawal Queue:** Ensure you’re reducing the number of pending invitations and withdrawals regularly. A high pending queue can lead to restrictions or even temporary bans. Consider withdrawing invites that aren't accepted after a reasonable period (e.g., 1–2 weeks).\n    90→- **Connection Rate:** Your connection conversion rate is excellent, but if the withdrawal queue remains high, it could affect future outreach. Make sure to focus on the balance between invitations and removals.\n    91→\n    92→### Optional Tool: LinkedHelper\n    93→\n    94→If you're looking for an alternative or additional tool, consider **LinkedHelper**. Export **companies** (no people yet).\n    19→    2. Filter companies in **Crona** to ICP using web processing.\n    20→        \n    21→        [Crona ](Collecting%20the%20database/Crona%20265d8691cb4680bbb539f22d55202607.md)\n    22→        \n    23→    3. Pull **people** only from the filtered set.\n    24→\n    25→## 3) Alt/Complementary Sources\n    26→\n    27→- **Sales Navigator + PhantomBuster** (incl. events). → [How-to](https://www.notion.so/caed0db2805349d186a1f9e5c9adb2c6?pvs=21)\n    28→- **Waalaxy** (fast LI extraction; good free tier).\n    29→- **Crunchbase** (funding signals). → [Guide](https://www.notion.so/1b2d8691cb468040ad3cc3723ac7b942?pvs=21)\n    30→- Explee - has advanced ai filters [Explee](Collecting%20the%20database/Explee%2026cd8691cb4680bf8816e5f4d3e8e448.md)\n    31→- **Scripts** (domain finder):\n    32→    - If you **only have names**, first run the **domain script** to resolve each company’s domain → **then** add to **Apollo** for enrichment (people, emails).\n    33→    - [Scripts](https://www.notion.so/852fb2b5c94f43b2aaabd371aed2b69c?pvs=21)\n    34→\n    35→## 4) Enrichment & Presets\n    36→\n    37→- **Clay** for enrichment (emails, LI URLs, company info, competitors).\n    38→    - If you only have **LinkedIn profile URLs**, use Clay’s **LinkedIn Profile** block to pull name/title/company/location.\n    39→    - [Clay guide](Collecting%20the%20database/Clay%20guide%201b2d8691cb4680f79ab8da20aa8084f9.md)\n    40→- **Crona Presets** for reusable segment filters. → [Crona](Collecting%20the%20database/Crona%20265d8691cb4680bbb539f22d55202607.md). It’s our own software use it!\n    41→\n    42→**Normalization (Crona + Sheets AI)**\n    43→\n    44→**Have existing company list from Apollo/other?**\n    45→\n    46→**Actively prospecting through web processing /Sales Navigator processing in crona?**\n    47→→ Use **Crona enrichers** \n    48→\n    49→**Key difference:** Crona normalizes as you prospect, Sheets normalizes existing data.\n    50→\n    51→## 5) Finding & Validating Emails (mandatory)\n    52→\n    53→- **Find emails**: **Clay** or **Findymail** (in Access).\n    54→    - How-to (Clay): [link](https://www.notion.so/118d8691cb46803fbc5fffccd69c04ba?pvs=21)\n    55→- **Validate** every list with **MillionVerifier** before sending.\n    56→\n    57→**Flow:** Source → (If names-only: **Script → Apollo enrich**) → Enrich (Clay/Findymail) → **Verify (MillionVerifier)** → Send.\n    58→\n    59→## 6) Mini SOP\n    60→\n    61→1. Check **Ready-Made Segments**.\n    62→2. Align **ICP** in shared sheet.\n    63→3. **If names-only**: run **domain script**, then **enrich in Apollo**.\n    64→4. **Apollo** companies → refine in **Crona** → pull people.\n    65→5. Fill gaps via **Sales Nav + PhantomBuster / Waalaxy / Crunchbase**.\n    66→6. **Clay/Findymail** for emails → **MillionVerifier** to clean.\n    67→7. Hand off clean CSV to outreach.\n    68→\n    69→[Clay guide](Collecting%20the%20database/Clay%20guide%201b2d8691cb4680f79ab8da20aa8084f9.md)\n    70→\n    71→## Target Russian speaking contacts\n 169→\n   170→Once you’ve exported a  base from any source — **don’t just trust it blindly**.\n   171→\n   172→- **Use filters** on key columns like `Industry`, `Keywords`, or `Headcount`.\n   173→- **Check for match with your original targeting** — for example, filter by the keywords you used in Apollo to see how many companies actually match.\n   174→- Use **“does not contain” filters** to catch and remove irrelevant companies (e.g. based on stop-words like \"Insurance\", \"Real Estate\", \"Logistics\" — depending on your case).\n   175→- If you spot suspicious clusters — e.g. lots of empty fields or mismatched industries — dig deeper or flag it.\n   176→\n   177→✅ Why this works better:\n   178→\n   179→– Gives you **quantitative clarity** on the quality of your base\n   180→\n   181→– Helps clean up irrelevant junk before launch\n   182→\n   183→– Lets you adjust your Apollo query if needed\n   184→\n   185→In addition to filtering in Google Sheets, it’s still worth manually opening a **random sample of ~20 company websites** from your base.\n   186→\n   187→## Conferences\n   188→\n   189→## Existing base\n   190→\n   191→Conferences are a powerful source of **high-intent leads** — attendees are often actively exploring new solutions.\n   192→\n   193→You can work with a base collected from past events \n   194→\n   195→[https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1ArNLCkDpiSYQZj5OnYio-QqlQznm0fyPr1oIpJV-YfA/edit?gid=1952588758#gid=1952588758](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1ArNLCkDpiSYQZj5OnYio-QqlQznm0fyPr1oIpJV-YfA/edit?gid=1952588758#gid=1952588758)\n   196→\n   197→<aside>\n   198→💡\n   199→\n   200→Format: \n   201→\n   202→- **Full Name** – имя и фамилия\n   203→- **Job Title** – должность\n   204→- **Company Name** – название компании\n   205→- **Email** – рабочая почта\n   206→- **LinkedIn Profile** – желательно, но не обязательно\n   207→- **Country** – страна/регион (если известен)\n   208→\n   209→- **Conference Name** – название конференции\n   210→- **Conference URL** – ссылка на сайт или страницу ивента\n   211→- **Conference Type** – офлайн / онлайн / гибрид\n   212→- Sector\n   213→- Country\n   214→- **Conference Date** – дата проведения\n   215→</aside>\n   216→\n   217→## Conferences process\n   218→\n   219→## The Main Decision: Is Your Client Attending?\n   220→\n   221→### ✅ Your Client IS Attending the Conference\n   222→\n   223→**Primary Goal:** Book face-to-face meetings at the event\n   224→\n   225→**Your Action Plan:**\n   226→\n   227→1. **Focus on Meeting Coordination** (Section 3)\n   228→    - Pre-book meetings before the event\n   229→    - Create shared calendar and communication group\n   230→    - Manage day-of logistics and follow-ups\n   231→2. **Use Conference App Messaging** (Section 2)\n   232→    - Send automated messages through the conference platform\n   233→    - Great for last-minute meeting requests\n   234→3. **Supplement with Online Research** (Section 1)\n   235→    - Build backup lists from LinkedIn and other sources\n   236→\n   237→### ❌ Your Client is NOT Attending the Conference\n   238→\n   239→**Primary Goal:** Build contact lists and reach out remotely\n   240→\n   241→**Your Action Plan:**\n   242→\n   243→1. **Use Conference App Messaging** (Section 2) - if the conference has a messaging system\n   244→2. **Focus on Online Research and Outreach** (Section 1)\n   245→\n   246→---\n   247→\n   248→## Section 1: Online Research & Outreach (Remote Strategy)\n   249→\n   250→**Step 1: Scrape the conference**\n   251→\n   252→*Scenario A: Direct People Scraping*\n   253→\n   254→**What this looks like:**\n   255→\n   256→- Conference website has a public attendee directory\n   257→- You can see individual names, job titles, and sometimes contact info\n   258→- LinkedIn Sales Navigator shows \"People who attended [Conference Name]\"\n   259→- Conference app displays attendee profiles directly\n   260→\n   261→**Tools to use:**\n   262→\n   263→- **PhantomBuster** - LinkedIn Events Attendees scraper\n   264→- **Octoparse** - Website scraping for public attendee lists\n   265→- **Waalaxy** - Quick LinkedIn profile extraction\n   266→- **Manual copying** - For smaller lists\n   267→\n   268→**Step-by-step process:**\n   269→\n   270→1. **Check the conference website**\n   271→    - Look for \"Attendees,\" \"Participants,\" or \"Directory\" sections\n   272→    - Some conferences show speaker lists, sponsor contacts, or networking directories\n   273→    - Use Octoparse to scrape if the list is large\n   274→    - Copy manually if it's a small list (under 50 people)\n   275→2. **Use the conference mobile app**\n   276→    - Download the event app if available\n   277→    - Many apps have attendee directories or networking features\n   278→    - Screenshot or manually copy contact information\n   279→    - Note: Some apps allow direct messaging (covered in Section 2)\n   280→    \n   281→    **Review these guides**\n   282→    \n   283→    [SBC **Summit conference scraping** (1)](Collecting%20the%20database/SBC%20Summit%20conference%20scraping%20(1)%20269d8691cb468028b5bbf6bebcd19bd4.md)\n   284→    \n   285→    ‣ \n   286→    \n   287→\n   288→*Scenario B: Company-First Scraping*\n   289→\n   290→**What this looks like:**\n   291→\n   292→- No direct attendee list available\n   293→- Conference shows sponsors, exhibitors, or speaking companies\n   294→- You can find companies but need to research people separately via apollo ([review)](Collecting%20the%20database%201bad8691cb4680ddb344febf68bccca6.md)\n   295→\n   296→---\n   297→\n   298→## Section 2: Conference App Messaging\n   299→\n   300→### When to Use This\n   301→\n   302→Use when the conference has its own app or website where attendees can message each other.\n   303→\n   304→**Review these guides**\n   305→\n   306→[SBC **Summit conference scraping**](Collecting%20the%20database/SBC%20Summit%20conference%20scraping%2025ad8691cb46808aa9c0c818a7433ea2.md)\n   307→\n   308→‣ \n   309→\n   310→### Setup Process\n   311→\n   312→**Step 1: Access the Conference Platform**\n   313→\n   314→- Log in to the conference app/website\n   315→- Ensure you can access the attendee directory and messaging features\n   316→\n   317→**Step 2: Filter Your Targets**\n   318→\n   319→- Find people who match your ideal customer profile\n   320→\n   321→**Step 3: Set Up Automated Messaging**\n   322→\n   323→- Use Octoparse software in Standard Mode\n   324→- Create one short paragraph message (no line breaks)\n   325→- Set up duplicate protection to avoid messaging the same person twice\n   326→- Enable automatic sending with 5-second delays\n   327→\n   328→**Message Template Example:**\n   329→\"Hey [FirstName], saw you're at [Event]. We help [company type] improve [specific benefit]. Quick intro this week to see if there's a fit?\"\n   330→\n   331→---\n   332→\n   333→## Section 3: In-Person Event Strategy (When Your Client Attends)\n   334→\n   335→### Goal\n   336→\n   337→Convert your presence at the event into qualified sales meetings through systematic pre-booking and day-of coordination.\n   338→\n   339→### Pre-Event (2 Weeks Before to Day Before)\n   340→\n   341→**Create Your Target List**\n   342→\n   343→- Identify 50-150 priority companies attending\n   344→- Map out key contacts (CEOs, VPs, Business Development)\n   345→\n   346→**Pre-Book Meetings**\n   347→\n   348→- Start LinkedIn outreach 2 weeks early\n   349→- Send targeted emails to key prospects\n   350→- Create a simple one-page company overview\n   351→- Prepare a 30-second pitch about your services\n   352→\n   353→**Set Up Operations**\n   354→\n   355→- Create a shared calendar with your client\n   356→- Set up a group chat (Telegram/WhatsApp) for real-time coordination\n   357→- Create a tracking sheet with: Company | Contact Name | Job Title | Meeting Time | Location | Owner | Status | Next Steps\n   358→\n   359→### During the Event (Each Day)\n   360→\n   361→**Morning Coordination (10 minutes)**\n   362→\n   363→- Review who you must meet today\n   364→- Confirm times and locations\n   365→- Identify gaps and fill with last-minute outreach\n   366→\n   367→**Meeting Management**\n   368→\n   369→- Every meeting gets a calendar invite\n   370→- Send reminders 30, 15, and 5 minutes before each meeting\n   371→- Coordinate via group chat if people are running late\n   372→\n   373→**Capture Information Quickly**\n   374→After each conversation, note:\n   375→\n   376→- What they need\n   377→- Any objections or concerns\n   378→- What they committed to\n   379→- Next steps\n   380→- Who owns the follow-up\n   381→\n   382→### After the Event (1-5 Days Later)\n   383→\n   384→- Send same-day or next-day follow-up emails with meeting recap\n   385→- Move contacts into your regular outreach sequences\n   386→- Attempt to reschedule no-shows (2 attempts max)\n   387→- Update tracking sheet with qualification status and next steps\n   388→\n   389→---\n   390→\n   391→## Another high intent sources\n   392→\n   393→[Explee](Collecting%20the%20database/Explee%2026cd8691cb4680bf8816e5f4d3e8e448.md)\n   394→\n 26→- Точно что написал (дословно важно — особенно если предложил время или задал вопрос)\n    27→- Чем занимается компания — для персонализации первой строки\n    28→\n    29→**Шаг 3 — Напиши ответ**\n    30→\n    31→Правила (из реальных успешных replies):\n    32→- **2-4 предложения** — не больше\n    33→- **Первая строка = ответ на их конкретную реплику**, не \"Thanks for your reply\"\n    34→- **Если предложили время → подтверди это время** (не посылай просто calendar link)\n    35→- **Если спросили вопрос → ответь прямо**, потом предложи call\n    36→- **Зеркали язык**: если for me. Good luck with {their tool/project}.\n   128→\n   129→Bhaskar\n   130→```\n   131→*→ Action: mark as \"not now\", add 3-month follow-up reminder*\n   132→\n   133→### not_interested — агрессивный / spam complaint\n   134→*→ Action: remove from ALL campaigns immediately. Финал — измеримый или качественный результат (\"flawless single-day installation\").\n    42→\n    43→4. **Призыв к действию (Call To Action)**\n    44→   - Мягкий, с низким барьером для входа.\n    45→   - Имя + Компания.\n    50→   - Упоминание 2-3 известных клиентов (social proof) для повышения доверия.\n    51→\n    52→---\n    53→\n    54→## Универсальные паттерны для адаптации\n    55→\n    56→При создании письма для любого проекта используйте следующий чек-лист:\n    57→\n    58→1. **Subject:** Оффер, направленный на решение конкретной задачи клиента (не вопрос).\n    59→2. **Параграф 1:** Боль целевого сегмента → ваше решение (ровно одна строка).\n    60→3. **Кейс:** Цифры + имя клиента + неожиданный факт или преодоленная сложность + итоговый результат.\n    61→4. **CTA:** Запрос на короткий промежуток времени (\"10 минут\") + обсуждение конкретного шага/процесса.\n    62→5. **Подпись:** Ваше имя + компания + 2–3 релевантных клиента из той же или смежной ниши (если есть).\n    63→"}]},"uuid":"6c1be6bd-c4fa-4dba-8575-4222dcbcff87","timestamp":"2026-03-26T09:45:48.530Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"b64b5a7d-7d23-44e1-86cd-6dced3ad5169","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/user/Library/Mobile Documents/com~apple~CloudDocs/sales_engineer/magnum-opus","sessionId":"f93e3293-8715-4c5d-b2be-af4a374c0fe7","version":"2.1.83","gitBranch":"main","slug":"effervescent-dreaming-dream"}

The limit per single search is **5,000 records**, but through multiple searches you can load 10,000, 20,000, 50,000 — all into one table.\n     8→\n     9→---\n    10→\n    11→## 1. Finding Companies (Find Leads)\n    12→\n    13→1. Click **Find Leads**\n    14→2. Choose: search by **companies** or by **people**\n    15→   - Companies usually work better — more custom filters (revenue, etc.)\n    16→   - People search works too, just fewer filters available\n    17→3. Set up filters (location, size, funding, etc.)\n    18→\n    19→### Example\n    20→\n    21→Goal: find founders of large businesses in the UAE.\n    22→\n    23→- Set location — UAE\n    24→- Result: 938 companies (narrow filters) or 10,000 (broad filters)\n    25→\n    26→---\n    27→\n    28→## 2. Bypassing the 5,000 Record Limit\n    29→\n    30→If results exceed 5,000:\n    31→\n    32→1. **First search** — narrow filters to get ≤ 5,000 records\n    33→   - E.g., companies with revenue from X to Y\n    34→2. **Export** to a new table (creates a Workbook)\n    35→3. **Second search** — adjust filters to the next range\n    36→   - E.g., revenue from Y to Z\n    37→4. **Export to the same table** — select **Save to existing table**\n    38→5. Repeat until everything is exported\n    39→\n    40→> Rename your Workbook immediately to stay organized. E.g.: \"Dubai Companies\"\n    41→\n    42→**How to split into batches:**\n    43→- By revenue ranges\n    44→- By company size (employee count)\n    45→- By other filters that yield batches ≤ 5,000\n    46→\n    47→---\n    48→\n    49→## 3. Finding People (Find People)\n    50→\n    51→After exporting companies, find people within them:\n    52→\n    53→1. **Find People** from the companies table\n    54→2. Filters:\n    55→   - **Job title** — C-Suite (exclude managers, assistants)\n    56→   - **Location** — e.g., UAE\n    57→3. Export to a new table\n    58→\n    59→If people > 5,000 — split by job titles and export in batches into the same table.\n    60→\n    61→### Visualization\n    62→\n    63→The **Overview** tab shows the entire pipeline:\n    64→- 2 company searches → 10,000 companies\n    65→- CEO search → results in people table\n    66→\n    67→---\n    68→\n    69→## 4. Enrichment\n    70→\n    71→### Email via FindyMail\n    72→\n    73→1. Add enrichment → **FindyMail**\n    74→2. Select **Find work email**\n    75→3. Click **Continue** → **Run**\n    76→\n    77→> **Important:** Use your own API key to avoid spending shared Clay credits.\n    78→\n    79→### AI Enrichment\n    80→\n    81→1. Add AI enrichment\n    82→2. Connect your own API key (ask Amir — he'll provide one with a limit)\n    83→3. Choose a model (GPT-4 or higher)\n    84→4. Кампании уходят с одинаковыми шаблонами для разных сегментов.\n\n2. **Нет шага \"25 компаний руками\".** Sally: \"You should take this process by iteration. Crona_guide_transcr/???cold_email_example.md`:\n- Subject = **конкретный оффер**, сразу понятна польза\n- \"Без интриги и кликбейта\"\n- Персонализация через `{company name}`\n- Пример: \"Receiving hub for {company name} projects\"\n\n### Текущие subjects OnSocial\n\nПо названиям кампаний и данным аудита (`sofia/smartlead-hub/onsocial_campaign_audit_2026-03-26.md`), OnSocial использует что-то вроде \"Creator data API for {company}\".\n\n### Проблемы\n\n1. **Один subject на все сегменты.** Sally требует разные subjects для INFLUENCER_PLATFORMS vs IM_FIRST_AGENCIES vs AFFILIATE_PERFORMANCE. \"Creator data API\" резонирует с платформами, но не с агентствами (агентства не думают в терминах API).\n\n2. **Слишком абстрактно.** Sally: \"конкретный оффер, сразу понятна польза.\" \"Creator data API\" описывает ЧТО, а не ЗАЧЕМ. Лучше: для агентств — \"Find verified creators for {company}'s campaigns\" / для платформ — \"Real-time creator analytics for {company}\".\n\n3. **A/B тестирование.** Sally (`Email outreach` файл, строка 80-81): \"Smartlead lets you A/B test multiple versions — Try creating 2 variations of your first message with different subject lines.\" По аудиту нет признаков A/B тестирования subjects.\n\n### Действие\n\n- Создать subject templates per segment (минимум 3 варианта на сегмент)\n- Запустить A/B тест subjects в SmartLead\n- Формулировать через пользу, а не через фичу\n\n---\n\n## 4. ОБРАБОТКА ОТВЕТОВ\n\n### Reply-OnSocial skill\n\nФайл: `sofia/skills/reply-onsocial.md`\n\nПокрывает 8 типов: interested, meeting_request, question, not_interested, ooo, wrong_person + подвиды (2 meeting_request, 2 not_interested).\n\n### Что говорит Sally\n\n- `Email outreach` файл, строка 133-147: \"SmartLead sometimes misses responses\" → использовать внешний email-клиент (Thunderbird/Spark)\n- Subsequence setup (строка 100-102)\n- Правило 500 писем без warm = пауза\n\n### Пробелы в reply-onsocial\n\n1. **Нет типа `referral_to_demo_link`.** Если лид сам шлет ссылку на свой calendly / предлагает demo их продукта (путая direction), нет шаблона.\n\n2. **Нет типа `ask_for_case_study`.** Когда лид просит \"do you have case studies?\" или \"who else uses this?\" — это не просто \"question\", это отдельный high-intent сигнал.\n\n3. **Нет обработки \"forward to team member\" (internal forward).** Когда лид пишет \"I'm forwarding this to our [role]\" — это не wrong_person, это warm signal с другим action.\n\n4. **Нет мониторинга через Thunderbird/Spark.** Sally прямо говорит, что SmartLead пропускает ответы — нужен внешний email-клиент. По аудиту, OnSocial не настроил это.\n\n5. **Нет автоматических subsequences.** Sally требует subsequence настройку — OnSocial не использует.\n\n### Действие\n\n- Добавить 3 типа: `case_study_request`, `internal_forward`, `confused_direction`\n- Настроить Thunderbird/Spark для 14 email-аккаунтов OnSocial\n- Настроить subsequences в SmartLead\n\n---\n\n## 5. ПАЙПЛАЙН СБОРА ДАННЫХ\n\n### Sally: полный pipeline\n\nФайл: `sofia/outreach_full_guide/Outreach full guide/Collecting the database 1bad8691cb4680ddb344febf68bccca6.md`\n\n```\n1. Check Ready-Made Segments\n2. Align ICP (shared sheet с клиентом)\n3. Apollo companies export\n4. Crona/pipeline segmentation\n5. Pull people from filtered set\n6. Clay/FindyMail → email enrichment\n7. MillionVerifier → validation\n8. SmartLead upload\n```\n\nДополнительно:\n- Conferences как high-intent source\n- Sales Navigator + PhantomBuster\n- Blacklist check через Google Sheets формулу\n- **\"25 companies per segment manually verified before launch\"** (из Collecting the database, строка 185)\n- Russian-speaking contacts как высококонверсионный сегмент\n\n### OnSocial GOD pipeline (Steps 0-11)\n\n```\nStep 0: Blacklist\nStep 1: Load & Normalize (из Google Sheets)\nStep 2: Dedup\nStep 3: Industry filter\nStep 4: Positive signal filter / FSA filter\nStep 5: DNS check\nStep 6: Scrape websites\nStep 6.5: Regexp pre-filter (parked, dead)\nStep 6.7: Deep scrape (retry failed)\nStep 7: GPT classification\nStep 8: Output (targets/rejects)\nStep 9: Apollo People Search\nStep 10: FindyMail enrichment\nStep 11: SmartLead upload\n```\n\n### Что OnSocial пропускает\n\n1. **Нет MillionVerifier.** Sally (строка 8-10, Email outreach): \"ALWAYS run lists through MillionVerifier before sending — even if sourced from trusted tools.\" GOD pipeline идет FindyMail → SmartLead без валидации. Это критично — FindyMail находит email, но не валидирует его на bounceability.\n\n2. **Нет ICP sheet с клиентом.** Sally: \"Share the ICP sheet with client → Only after ICP: Approved → collect companies.\" OnSocial начал собирать без формального ICP alignment.\n\n3. **Нет альтернативных источников.** Sally использует Sales Navigator, PhantomBuster, Waalaxy, Crunchbase, конференции. OnSocial — только Apollo export. При 14,900 компаний и 4.8% target rate (719/14900), расширение источников могло бы добавить qualifed leads.\n\n4. **Нет #review-sequences.** Sally (Email outreach, строка 40): \"drop them into the #review-sequences Slack channel.\" OnSocial не имеет peer review sequences.\n\n5. **Нет еженедельной очистки.** Sally (строка 104-130): \"Remove old leads from Smartlead every Friday.\" По аудиту, paused кампании с ~18,679 лидами висят мертвым грузом.\n\n### Действие\n\n- Добавить MillionVerifier как Step 10.5 (между FindyMail и SmartLead)\n- Каждую пятницу: экспорт + удаление из paused кампаний\n- Рассмотреть конференции (SBC Summit и т.д.) как источник high-intent leads для influencer marketing\n\n---\n\n## 6. КОНТРОЛЬНЫЕ ТОЧКИ КАЧЕСТВА\n\n### Правило Sally\n\n1. **\"25 companies per segment manually verified before launch\"** — из `Collecting the database`, строка 185: \"manually opening a random sample of ~20 company websites\"\n2. **\"500 emails → 0 warm = pause\"** — из `Email outreach`, строка 82-83\n\n### Что делает OnSocial\n\nПо аудиту (`onsocial_campaign_audit_2026-03-26.md`):\n\n**Правило 500 писем:**\n- `0903_PLATFORMS`: 915 sent, 0 positive — **НАРУШЕНИЕ** (должна была быть пауза при 500)\n- `0903_AGENCIES`: 1,122 sent, 0 positive — **НАРУШЕНИЕ**\n- `MARKETING_AGENCIES`: 604 sent, 0 positive — **НАРУШЕНИЕ**\n- `1103_PR_firms`: 433 sent, 0 positive — приближается к границе\n\nИз 19 кампаний, **3 кампании прямо нарушают правило 500-и-стоп**, отправив суммарно ~2,641 писем в пустоту.\n\n**Правило 25 компаний:**\n- Pipeline имеет `--validate N` флаг, но нет доказательства что он использовался перед каждым запуском\n- Нет документированного процесса ручной проверки 25 компаний per segment\n\n### Действие\n\n- Немедленно: отключить 0903_PLATFORMS, 0903_AGENCIES, MARKETING_AGENCIES (рекомендация уже в аудите)\n- Автоматизировать: добавить в SmartLead webhook/cron проверку \"500 sent, 0 warm reply → auto-pause\"\n- Формализовать: перед каждым Step 11 (SmartLead upload) — обязательный manual review 25 random targets из Step 8\n\n---\n\n## СВОДКА ПРИОРИТЕТОВ\n\n| #
